Task instruction sent to agent 
# Support CockroachDB as a First-Class Database Backend

**Repository:** flipt-io/flipt
**Language:** Go
**Difficulty:** hard

## Problem

CockroachDB uses the same wire protocol as PostgreSQL, allowing it to work with existing PostgreSQL-compatible drivers. However, Flipt does not recognize CockroachDB as a distinct backend in configuration or database migrations. Flipt's internal logic currently assumes PostgreSQL when using the Postgres driver, which causes issues when targeting CockroachDB without explicit support. This prevents seamless setup and deployment of Flipt with CockroachDB, even though technical compatibility exists.

## Key Components

- Configuration parsing — where database protocol/driver is resolved from config
- Database migration logic — uses `golang-migrate` with driver-specific handling
- SQL driver initialization — where the PostgreSQL driver is selected and configured

## Task

1. Add `cockroachdb` as a supported database protocol in Flipt's configuration schema
2. Enable migrations using the CockroachDB driver in `golang-migrate`
3. Ensure the CockroachDB backend reuses PostgreSQL SQL driver logic where appropriate
4. Add or update configuration validation to accept the new backend
5. Run existing tests to ensure no regressions with PostgreSQL and other backends

## Success Criteria

- `cockroachdb` is accepted as a valid database protocol in configuration
- Migrations run correctly with the CockroachDB driver
- CockroachDB backend shares appropriate SQL logic with the PostgreSQL backend
- Existing database backends (PostgreSQL, MySQL, SQLite) are unaffected
- All existing tests pass

    12→func runMigrations(cfg *config.Config, logger *zap.Logger) error {
    13→	var (
    14→		migrator *analytics.Migrator
    15→		err      error
    16→	)
    17→
    18→	migrator, err = analytics.NewMigrator(*cfg, logger)
    19→	if err != nil {
    20→		return err
    21→	}
    22→
    23→	defer migrator.Close()
    24→
    25→	if err := migrator.Up(true); err != nil {
    26→		return fmt.Errorf("running migrator %w", err)
    27→	}
    28→
    29→	return nil
    30→}
    31→
    32→func newMigrateCommand() *cobra.Command {
    33→	cmd := &cobra.Command{
    34→		Use:   "migrate",
    35→		Short: "Run pending database migrations",
    36→		RunE: func(cmd *cobra.Command, _ []string) error {
    37→			ctx := cmd.Context()
    38→			logger, cfg, err := buildConfig(ctx)
    39→			if err != nil {
    40→				return err
    41→			}
    42→
    43→			defer func() {
    44→				_ = logger.Sync()
    45→			}()
    46→
    47→			if err := runMigrations(cfg, logger); err != nil {
    48→				return err
    49→			}
    50→
    51→			return nil
    52→		},
    53→	}
    54→
    55→	cmd.Flags().StringVar(&providedConfigFile, "config", "", "path to config file")
    56→	return cmd
    57→}

    29→func migratorHelper(logger *zap.Logger, db *sql.DB, driver Driver, databaseDriver database.Driver) (*Migrator, error) {
    30→	// source migrations from embedded config/migrations package

    34→		return nil, err
    35→	}
    36→
    37→	mm, err := migrate.NewWithInstance("iofs", sourceDriver, driver.Migrations(), databaseDriver)
    38→	if err != nil {
    39→		return nil, fmt.Errorf("creating migrate instance: %w", err)
    40→	}
    41→
    42→	return &Migrator{
    43→		db:       db,
    44→		migrator: mm,
    45→		logger:   logger,
    46→		driver:   driver,
    47→	}, nil
    48→}

    11→
    12→// open is a convenience function of providing a database.sql instance for
    13→// an analytics database.
    14→func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
    15→	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
    16→		clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
    17→		if err != nil {
    18→			return nil, "", err
    19→		}
    20→
    21→		db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)
    22→
    23→		return db, Clickhouse, nil
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
    27→}
    28→

    32→	}

    13→	// Flipt application.

    15→	version:         "2.0" | *"2.0"
    16→	experimental?:   #experimental
    17→	analytics?:      #analytics
    18→	authentication?: #authentication
    19→	authorization?:  #authorization
    20→	cors?:           #cors
    21→	diagnostics?:    #diagnostics
    22→	evaluation?:     #evaluation
    23→	environments?:   #environments
    24→	storage?:        #storage
    25→	templates?:      #templates
    26→	credentials?:    #credentials
    27→	log?:            #log
    28→	meta?:           #meta
    29→	server?:         #server
    30→	metrics?:        #metrics
    31→	tracing?:        #tracing
    32→	ui?:             #ui
    33→	license?:        #license
    34→	secrets?:        #secrets
    35→
    36→	#authentication: {
    37→		required?: bool | *false
    38→		exclude?: {
    39→			management: bool | *false
    40→			metadata:   bool | *false
    41→			evaluation: bool | *false
    42→			ofrep:      bool | *false
    43→		}
    44→
    45→		session?: {
    46→			domain?:        string
    47→			secure?:        bool
    48→			token_lifetime: =~#duration | *"24h"
    49→			state_lifetime: =~#duration | *"10m"
    50→			csrf?: {
    51→				key:    string

     7→## Project Overview

    10→
    11→- **v1 code**: Located on `main` branch
    12→- **v2 code**: Located on current (`v2`) branch. This is the default branch in the repository.

    14→- **Requirements**: Go 1.25+ and Node.js 18+
    15→
    16→## Project Architecture & Structure
    17→
    18→### Repository Structure
    19→
    20→- `cmd/flipt/` - Main application entry point
    21→- `core/` - Core validation and business logic
    22→- `errors/` - Shared error definitions
    23→- `internal/` - Core application logic (not importable)
    24→  - `cmd/` - Internal command utilities and code generation tools
    25→  - `common/` - Shared types and utilities across internal packages
    26→  - `config/` - Configuration management
    27→  - `containers/` - Container test utilities
    28→  - `coss/` - Commercial open source features (license management, enterprise storage, secrets)
    29→  - `secrets/` - Secret management system with provider interface (OSS file provider, Pro Vault provider)
    30→  - `credentials/` - Credential management for cloud storage and Git authentication
    31→  - `ext/` - Import/export functionality for flags and segments
    32→  - `gateway/` - HTTP gateway implementation
    33→  - `info/` - Version and build information
    34→  - `migrations/` - Database

package config

import (
	"encoding/json"
	"time"

	"github.com/spf13/viper"
)

const (
	// configuration keys
	dbURL             = "db.url"
	dbMigrationsPath  = "db.migrations.path"
	dbMaxIdleConn     = "db.max_idle_conn"
	dbMaxOpenConn     = "db.max_open_conn"
	dbConnMaxLifetime = "db.conn_max_lifetime"
	dbName            = "db.name"
	dbUser            = "db.user"
	dbPassword        = "db.password"
	dbHost            = "db.host"
	dbPort            = "db.port"
	dbProtocol        = "db.protocol"

	// database protocol enum
	_ DatabaseProtocol = iota
	// DatabaseSQLite ...
	DatabaseSQLite
	// DatabasePostgres ...
	DatabasePostgres
	// DatabaseMySQL ...
	DatabaseMySQL
	// DatabaseCockroachDB ...
	DatabaseCockroachDB
)

// DatabaseConfig contains fields, which configure the various relational database backends.
//
// Flipt currently supports SQLite, Postgres and MySQL backends.
type DatabaseConfig struct {
	MigrationsPath  string           `json:"migrationsPath,omitempty"`
	URL             string           `json:"url,omitempty"`
	MaxIdleConn     int              `json:"maxIdleConn,omitempty"`
	MaxOpenConn     int              `json:"maxOpenConn,omitempty"`
	ConnMaxLifetime time.Duration    `json:"connMaxLifetime,omitempty"`
	Name            string           `json:"name,omitempty"`
	User            string           `json:"user,omitempty"`
	Password        string           `json:"password,omitempty"`
	Host            string           `json:"host,omitempty"`
	Port            int              `json:"port,omitempty"`
	Protocol        DatabaseProtocol `json:"protocol,omitempty"`
}

    37→// New constructs a new clickhouse client that conforms to the analytics.Client contract.
    38→func New(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) (*Client, error) {
    39→	var (
    40→		conn          *sql.DB
    41→		clickhouseErr error
    42→	)
    43→
    44→	dbOnce.Do(func() {
    45→		err := runMigrations(logger, cfg, forceMigrate)
    46→		if err != nil {
    47→			clickhouseErr = err
    48→			return
    49→		}
    50→
    51→		connection, err := connect(cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse)
    52→		if err != nil {
    53→			clickhouseErr = err
    54→			return
    55→		}
    56→
    57→		conn = connection
    58→	})
    59→
    60→	if clickhouseErr != nil {
    61→		return nil, clickhouseErr
    62→	}
    63→
    64→	return &Client{Conn: conn}, nil
    65→}

    27→// Installs tools required for development
    28→func Bootstrap() error {

    30→	for _, tool := range tools {
    31→		if tool == "./internal/cmd/protoc-gen-go-flipt-sdk/..." {
    32→			cmd := exec.Command("go", "install", ".")
    33→
    34→			cmd.Dir = "internal/cmd/protoc-gen-go-flipt-sdk"
    35→			cmd.Stdout = os.Stdout
    36→			cmd.Stderr = os.Stderr
    37→			if err := cmd.Run(); err != nil {
    38→				return fmt.Errorf("installing tool %q: %w", tool, err)
    39→			}
    40→			continue
    41→		}
    42→		if err := sh.RunV("go", "install", "-v", tool); err != nil {
    43→			return fmt.Errorf("installing tool %q: %w", tool, err)
    44→		}
    45→	}
    46→
    47→	return sh.RunV("go", "install", "tool")
    48→}

    56→		return err
    57→	}
    58→
    59→	fmt.Printf("\nRun the following to start Flipt:\n")
    60→	fmt.Printf("\n%v\n", color.CyanString(`./bin/flipt server [--config config/local.yml]`))
    61→	return nil
    62→}

     8→
     9→	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config"
    10→)
    11→
    12→// open is a convenience function of providing a database.sql instance for
    13→// an analytics database.
    14→func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
    15→	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
    16→		clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
    17→		if err != nil {
    18→			return nil, "", err
    19→		}
    20→
    21→		db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)
    22→
    23→		return db, Clickhouse, nil
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
    27→}
    28→
    29→var (
    30→	stringToDriver = map[string]Driver{
    31→		"clickhouse": Clickhouse,
    32→	}
    33→)
    34→
    35→// Driver represents a database driver
    36→type Driver string
    37→
    38→func (d Driver) String() string {
    39→	return string(d)
    40→}
    41→
    42→func (d Driver) Migrations() string {
    43→	return d.String()
    44→}
    45→
    46→const (
    47→	Clickhouse Driver = "clickhouse"
    48→)

    29→func migratorHelper(logger *zap.Logger, db *sql.DB, driver Driver, databaseDriver database.Driver) (*Migrator, error) {

    31→	// relative to the specific driver

    33→	if err != nil {
    34→		return nil, err
    35→	}
    36→
    37→	mm, err := migrate.NewWithInstance("iofs", sourceDriver, driver.Migrations(), databaseDriver)
    38→	if err != nil {
    39→		return nil, fmt.Errorf("creating migrate instance: %w", err)
    40→	}
    41→
    42→	return &Migrator{
    43→		db:       db,
    44→		migrator: mm,
    45→		logger:   logger,
    46→		driver:   driver,
    47→	}, nil
    48→}

    37→// New constructs a new clickhouse client that conforms to the analytics.Client contract.
    38→func New(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) (*Client, error) {
    39→	var (
    40→		conn          *sql.DB
    41→		clickhouseErr error
    42→	)
    43→
    44→	dbOnce.Do(func() {
    45→		err := runMigrations(logger, cfg, forceMigrate)
    46→		if err != nil {
    47→			clickhouseErr = err
    48→			return
    49→		}
    50→
    51→		connection, err := connect(cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse)
    52→		if err != nil {
    53→			clickhouseErr = err
    54→			return
    55→		}
    56→
    57→		conn = connection
    58→	})
    59→
    60→	if clickhouseErr != nil {
    61→		return nil, clickhouseErr
    62→	}
    63→
    64→	return &Client{Conn: conn}, nil
    65→}

     1→package analytics
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"database/sql/driver"
     5→	"encoding/json"
     6→	"fmt"
     7→	"time"
     8→
     9→	"google.golang.org/protobuf/types/known/timestamppb"
    10→)
    11→
    12→type Timestamp struct {
    13→	*timestamppb.Timestamp
    14→}
    15→
    16→func (t *Timestamp) Scan(value any) error {
    17→	if v, ok := value.(time.Time); ok {
    18→		val := timestamppb.New(v)
    19→		if err := val.CheckValid(); err != nil {
    20→			return err
    21→		}
    22→
    23→		t.Timestamp = val
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil
    27→}
    28→
    29→func (t *Timestamp) Value() (driver.Value, error) {
    30→	return t.Timestamp.AsTime(), t.Timestamp.CheckValid()
    31→}
    32→
    33→type NullableTimestamp Timestamp
    34→
    35→func (t *NullableTimestamp) Scan(value any) error {
    36→	if value == nil {
    37→		return nil
    38→	}
    39→
    40→	if v, ok := value.(time.Time); ok {
    41→		val := timestamppb.New(v)
    42→		if err := val.CheckValid(); err != nil {
    43→			return err
    44→		}
    45→
    46→		t.Timestamp = val
    47→	}
    48→
    49→	return nil
    50→}
    51→
    52→func (t *NullableTimestamp) Value() (driver.Value, error) {
    53→	if t.Timestamp == nil {
    54→		return nil, nil
    55→	}
    56→
    57→	return t.Timestamp.AsTime(), t.Timestamp.CheckValid()
    58→}
    59→
    60→type JSONField[T any] struct {
    61→	T T
    62→}
    63→
    64→func (f *JSONField[T]) Scan(v any) error {
    65→	if v == nil {
    66→		return nil
    67→	}
    68→
    69→	var bytes []byte
    70→	switch b := v.(type) {
    71→	case []byte:
    72→		bytes = b
    73→	case string:
    74→		bytes = []byte(b)
    75→	default:
    76→		return fmt.Errorf("unexpected type for data: %T", v)
    77→	}
    78→

    17→func (s *StoragesConfig) validate() error {

    19→		if err := storage.validate(); err != nil {
    20→			return errFieldWrap("storage", name, err)
    21→		}
    22→	}
    23→
    24→	return nil
    25→}
    26→
    27→func (s *StoragesConfig) setDefaults(v *viper.Viper) error {
    28→	storages, ok := v.AllSettings()["storage"].(map[string]any)
    29→	if !ok || len(storages) == 0 {
    30→		// Create default storage if no storages are configured
    31→		v.SetDefault("storage.default.name", "default")
    32→		v.SetDefault("storage.default.backend.type", "memory")
    33→		v.SetDefault("storage.default.branch", "main")
    34→		v.SetDefault("storage.default.poll_interval", "30s")
    35→		return nil
    36→	}

    39→		getString := func(s string) string {
    40→			return v.GetString("storage." + name + "." + s)
    41→		}
    42→
    43→		setDefault := func(k string, s any) {
    44→			v.SetDefault("storage."+name+"."+k, s)
    45→		}
    46→
    47→		setDefault("name", name)
    48→
    49→		switch getString("backend.type") {
    50→		case string(LocalStorageBackendType):
    51→			setDefault("backend.path", ".")
    52→		default:
    53→			setDefault("backend.type", "memory")
    54→		}
    55→
    56→		if getString("branch") == "" {
    57→			setDefault("branch", "main")
    58→		}
    59→
    60→		if getString("poll_interval") == "" {
    61→			setDefault("poll_int

## Summary: SQL Database Configuration and Drivers in Flipt Codebase

Based on my thorough search of the Flipt codebase, here are all the files dealing with SQL database configuration and connections. **Note: This is a v2 Git-native architecture that does NOT use PostgreSQL, MySQL, or SQLite for the main feature flag storage.** Instead, it uses Git repositories as the primary storage backend. However, ClickHouse (an OLAP database) is used for analytics data.

### SQL Database Files Found:

**Analytics/ClickHouse Database Configuration:**

1. **`/workspace/flipt/internal/storage/analytics/db.go`**
   - Main database initialization for analytics
   - ClickHouse driver setup using `github.com/ClickHouse/clickhouse-go/v2`
   - Opens database connections via `clickhouse.OpenDB()`

2. **`/workspace/flipt/internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go`**
   - Database schema migration handler for analytics
   - Uses `golang-migrate` library for database migrations
   - Implements `Migrator` struct for ClickHouse migrations
   - Migration version tracking

3. **`/workspace/flipt/internal/storage/analytics/fields.go`**
   - Custom SQL field types implementing `database/sql/driver.Valuer` and `database/sql.Scanner` interfaces
   - Implements custom types: `Timestamp`, `NullableTimestamp`, `JSONField[T]`
   - Handles value conversion between Go types and database types

4. **`/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/clickhouse/client.go`**
   - ClickHouse client implementation for analytics data retrieval
   - Uses `database/sql` package with `*sql.DB` connections
   - Implements query execution with `QueryContext()` and `Rows.Scan()`
   - Methods: `GetFlagEvaluationsCou

    11→
    12→// open is a convenience function of providing a database.sql instance for
    13→// an analytics database.
    14→func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
    15→	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
    16→		clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
    17→		if err != nil {
    18→			return nil, "", err
    19→		}
    20→
    21→		db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)
    22→
    23→		return db, Clickhouse, nil
    24→	}
    25→
    26→	return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
    27→}
    28→
    29→var (
    30→	stringToDriver = map[string]Driver{
    31→		"clickhouse": Clickhouse,
    32→	}
    33→)
    34→
    35→// Driver represents a database driver
    36→type Driver string
    37→
    38→func (d Driver) String() string {
    39→	return string(d)
    40→}
    41→
    42→func (d Driver) Migrations() string {
    43→	return d.String()
    44→}
    45→

    47→	Clickhouse Driver = "clickhouse"
    48→)

## Phase 1: Identify Changes

Use the Agent tool to launch all three agents concurrently in a single message. Pass each agent the full diff so it has the complete context.

### Agent 1: Code Reuse Review

For each change:

1. **Search for existing utilities and helpers** that could replace newly written code. Use Grep to find similar patterns elsewhere in the codebase — common locations are utility directories, shared modules, and files adjacent to the changed ones.
2. **Flag any new function that duplicates existing functionality.** Suggest the existing function to use instead.
3. **Flag any inline logic that could use an existing utility** — hand-rolled string manipulation, manual path handling, custom environment checks, ad-hoc type guards, and similar patterns are common candidates.

### Agent 2: Code Quality Review

Review the same changes for hacky patterns:

1. **Redundant state**: state that duplicates existing state, cached values that could be derived, observers/effects that could be direct calls
2. **Parameter sprawl**: adding new parameters to a function instead of generalizing or restructuring existing ones
3. **Copy-paste with slight variation**: near-duplicate code blocks that should be unified with a shared abstraction
4. **Leaky abstractions**: exposing internal details that should be encapsulated, or breaking existing abstraction boundaries

+package cockroachdb
+
+import (
+	"context"
+	"database/sql"
+	"fmt"
+	"sync"
+	"time"
+
+	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config"
+	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/server/analytics"
+	analyticsstorage "go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/storage/analytics"
+	"go.uber.org/zap"
+)
+
+var dbOnce sync.Once
+
+type Client struct {
+	Conn *sql.DB
+}
+
+// New constructs a new CockroachDB client that conforms to the analytics.Client contract.
+func New(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) (*Client, error) {
+	var (
+		conn          *sql.DB
+		cockroachErr  error
+	)
+
+	dbOnce.Do(func() {
+		err := runMigrations(logger, cfg, forceMigrate)
+		if err != nil {
+			cockroachErr = err
+			return
+		}
+
+		connection, err := connect(cfg.Analytics.Storage.CockroachDB)
+		if err != nil {
+			cockroachErr = err
+			return
+		}
+
+		conn = connection
+	})
+
+	if cockroachErr != nil {
+		return nil, cockroachErr
+	}
+
+	return &Client{Conn: conn}, nil
+}
+
+// runMigrations will run migrations for CockroachDB.
+func runMigrations(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) error {
+	m, err := analyticsstorage.NewMigrator(*cfg, logger)
+	if err != nil {
+		return err
+	}
+
+	if err := m.Up(forceMigrate); err != nil {
+		return err
+	}
+
+	return nil
+}
+
+func connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {
+	conn, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.URL)
+	if err != nil {
+		return nil, err
+	}
+
+	if err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {
+		return nil, err
+	}
+
+	return conn, nil
+}
+

+	ret

## Changes Summary

New CockroachDB analytics backend implementation with:
- Connection pooling via database/sql
- Migration handling with golang-migrate
- Query execution for flag evaluation analytics

## Task

Review for efficiency issues:

1. **Unnecessary work**:
   - Redundant computations (e.g., calculating time windows multiple times)
   - Repeated file reads or data lookups
   - Unnecessary type conversions

2. **Connection and pooling**:
   - Is sql.Open configured properly for connection pooling?
   - Missing connection pool size settings?
   - Unnecessary Ping() calls that could cause latency?

3. **Query efficiency**:
   - N+1 query patterns?
   - Inefficient query logic (e.g., large GROUP BY operations)?
   - Missing query parameters/prepared statements?
   - Unbounded result sets?

4. **Missed opportunities for concurrency**:
   - Can independent operations run in parallel?
   - Is sync.Once appropriate and safe?

5. **Hot-path bloat**:
   - Is blocking work being added to startup (migrations)?
   - Are migrations forced unnecessarily?

6. **Memory issues**:
   - Unbounded slices/arrays being allocated?
   - Memory leaks from connections or resources?
   - Unnecessary data copies?

7. **Startup performance**:
   - Is dbOnce.Do() efficient for one-time initialization?
   - Should migrations be optional or async?

    14→)

    18→type Client struct {
    19→	Conn *sql.DB
    20→}
    21→
    22→// New constructs a new CockroachDB client that conforms to the analytics.Client contract.
    23→func New(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) (*Client, error) {
    24→	var (
    25→		conn          *sql.DB
    26→		cockroachErr  error
    27→	)
    28→
    29→	dbOnce.Do(func() {
    30→		err := runMigrations(logger, cfg, forceMigrate)
    31→		if err != nil {
    32→			cockroachErr = err
    33→			return
    34→		}
    35→
    36→		connection, err := connect(cfg.Analytics.Storage.CockroachDB)
    37→		if err != nil {
    38→			cockroachErr = err
    39→			return
    40→		}
    41→
    42→		conn = connection
    43→	})
    44→
    45→	if cockroachErr != nil {
    46→		return nil, cockroachErr
    47→	}
    48→
    49→	return &Client{Conn: conn}, nil
    50→}
    51→
    52→// runMigrations will run migrations for CockroachDB.
    53→func runMigrations(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) error {
    54→	m, err := analyticsstorage.NewMigrator(*cfg, logger)
    55→	if err != nil {
    56→		return err
    57→	}
    58→
    59→	if err := m.Up(forceMigrate); err != nil {
    60→		return err
    61→	}
    62→
    63→	return nil
    64→}
    65→
    66→func connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {
    67→	conn, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.URL)
    68→	if e

    15→// AnalyticsStorageConfig is a collection of configuration option for storage backends.

    26→	}
    27→
    28→	if a.CockroachDB.Enabled {
    29→		return "cockroachdb"
    30→	}
    31→
    32→	if a.Prometheus.Enabled {
    33→		return "prometheus"
    34→	}
    35→	return ""
    36→}

     1→package analytics
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"database/sql"
     5→	"errors"
     6→	"fmt"
     7→
     8→	"github.com/ClickHouse/clickhouse-go/v2"
     9→	_ "github.com/lib/pq"

    11→	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config"
    12→)
    13→
    14→// open is a convenience function of providing a database.sql instance for
    15→// an analytics database.
    16→func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
    17→	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
    18→		clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
    19→		if err != nil {
    20→			return nil, "", err
    21→		}
    22→
    23→		db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)
    24→
    25→		return db, Clickhouse, nil
    26→	}
    27→
    28→	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.CockroachDB.Enabled {
    29→		db, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.Analytics.Storage.CockroachDB.URL)
    30→		if err != nil {
    31→			return nil, "", fmt.Errorf("failed to open CockroachDB connection: %w", err)
    32→		}
    33→
    34→		if err := db.Ping(); err != nil {
    35→			return nil, "", fmt.Errorf("failed to ping CockroachDB: %w", err)
    36→		}
    37→
    38→		return db, CockroachDB, nil
    39→	}
    40→
    41→	return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
    42→}
    43→
    44→var (
    45→	stringToDriver = map[string]Driver{
    46→		"clickhouse":  Clickhouse,
    47→		"cockroachdb": CockroachDB,
    48→		"cockroach":   CockroachDB,
    49→	}
    50→)

    57→}

    60→	return d.String()

     1→package analytics

     3→import (

     8→	"github.com/golang-migrate/migrate/v4"

    11→	postgresMigrate "github.com/golang-migrate/migrate/v4/database/postgres"
    12→	"github.com/golang-migrate/migrate/v4/source/iofs"
    13→	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config"
    14→	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/migrations"
    15→	"go.uber.org/zap"
    16→)
    17→
    18→var expectedVersions = map[Driver]uint{
    19→	Clickhouse:  3,
    20→	CockroachDB: 3,
    21→}
    22→
    23→// Migrator is responsible for migrating the database schema
    24→type Migrator struct {
    25→	db       *sql.DB
    26→	driver   Driver
    27→	logger   *zap.Logger
    28→	migrator *migrate.Migrate
    29→}
    30→
    31→func migratorHelper(logger *zap.Logger, db *sql.DB, driver Driver, databaseDriver database.Driver) (*Migrator, error) {
    32→	// source migrations from embedded config/migrations package
    33→	// relative to the specific driver
    34→	sourceDriver, err := iofs.New(migrations.FS, driver.Migrations())
    35→	if err != nil {
    36→		return nil, err
    37→	}
    38→
    39→	mm, err := migrate.NewWithInstance("iofs", sourceDriver, driver.Migrations(), databaseDriver)
    40→	if err != nil {
    41→		return nil, fmt.Errorf("creating migrate instance: %w", err)
    42→	}
    43→
    44→	return &Migrator{
    45→		db:       db,
    46→		migrator: mm,
    47→		logger:   logger,
    48→		driver:   driver,
    49→	}, nil
    50→}
    51→

    53→func NewMigrator(cfg config.Config, logger *zap.Logger) (*Migra
... (truncated)

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS flipt_counter_analytics_v2 (
    timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
    analytic_name VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    environment_key VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    namespace_key VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    flag_key VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    flag_type VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    reason VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    match BOOLEAN,
    evaluation_value VARCHAR,
    entity_id VARCHAR,
    value INT4 NOT NULL,
    PRIMARY KEY (timestamp, analytic_name, environment_key, namespace_key, flag_key)
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_flipt_counter_analytics_v2_timestamp ON flipt_counter_analytics_v2 (timestamp);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_flipt_counter_analytics_v2_env_ns_flag ON flipt_counter_analytics_v2 (environment_key, namespace_key, flag_key);
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2 (
    timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
    analytic_name VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    environment_key VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    namespace_key VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    flag_key VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    reason VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    evaluation_value VARCHAR,
    value INT4 NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
    PRIMARY KEY (timestamp, analytic_name, environment_key, namespace_key, flag_key, reason, evaluation_value)
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2_env_ns_flag ON flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2 (environment_key, namespace_key, flag_key);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2_timestamp ON flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2 (timestamp);
CREATE VIEW flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_mv_v2 AS
SELECT
    timestamp,
    analytic_name,
    environment_key,
    namespace_key,
    flag_key,
    reason,
    evaluation_value,
    SUM(value) AS value
FROM flipt_counter_analytics_v2
GROUP BY
    timestamp,
    analytic_name,
    environment_key,
    name

    55→		}

    58→	})

331-assistanttool_useBash
332-usertool_resultBash
	`,
		req.EnvironmentKey,
		req.NamespaceKey,
		req.FlagKey,
		req.StepMinutes,
		req.From,
		req.To,
	)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, nil, err
	}

	defer func() {
		_ = rows.Close()
	}()

	var (
		timestamps = make([]string, 0)
		values     = make([]float32, 0)
	)

	for rows.Next() {
		var (
			timestampBucket int64
			value           int32
		)

		if err := rows.Scan(&timestampBucket, &value); err != nil {
			return nil, nil, err
		}

		timestamp := time.Unix(timestampBucket, 0).UTC().Format(time.DateTime)
		timestamps = append(timestamps, timestamp)
		values = append(values, float32(value))
	}

	return timestamps, values, rows.Err()
}

// GetBatchFlagEvaluationsCount retrieves evaluation counts for multiple flags.
func (c *Client) GetBatchFlagEvaluationsCount(ctx context.Context, req *analytics.BatchFlagEvaluationsCountRequest) (map[string]analytics.FlagEvaluationData, error) {
	result := make(map[string]analytics.FlagEvaluationData)

	// Build the query with the provided flags
	query := `
		SELECT
			flag_key,
			EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM DATE_TRUNC('minute', timestamp))::bigint / ($4 * 60) * ($4 * 60) AS timestamp_bucket,
			SUM(value) AS value
		FROM flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2
		WHERE
			environment_key = $1 AND
			namespace_key = $2 AND
			flag_key = ANY($7) AND
			timestamp >= $5 AND
			timestamp < $6
		GROUP BY flag_key, timestamp_bucket
		ORDER BY flag_key, timestamp_bucket ASC
		LIMIT $8
	`

	rows, err := c.Conn.QueryContext(ctx, query,
		req.EnvironmentKey,
		req.NamespaceKey,
		nil, // placeholder for step (not needed in this query)
		req.StepMinutes,
		req.From,
		req.To,
		req.FlagKeys,
		req.Limit,
	)

Perfect. Now I have all the information I need to write a comprehensive efficiency review. Let me create the report:

## Code Efficiency Review: Flipt CockroachDB Analytics Backend

I've completed a thorough analysis of the CockroachDB analytics backend implementation. Below are my efficiency findings organized by category and severity.

---

## 1. CRITICAL EFFICIENCY ISSUES

### Issue 1.1: Missing Connection Pool Configuration
**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 66-77)

**Problem**: 
The `connect()` function uses `sql.Open()` without configuring connection pool parameters:
```go
func connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {
	conn, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.URL)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	if err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	return conn, nil
}
```

The default connection pool settings in Go's `database/sql` are:
- `MaxOpenConns`: unlimited (can cause resource exhaustion)
- `MaxIdleConns`: 2 (too low for analytics workloads)
- `ConnMaxLifetime`: unlimited (connections not recycled)

**Impact**: **HIGH** - For analytics workloads with multiple concurrent queries, this will:
- Create unbounded connections under load
- Exhaust database connection limits
- Cause connection pool starvation
- Lead to cascading failures

**Recommendation**:
```go
func connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {
	conn, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.URL)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	// Configure connection pool for analytics workloads
	conn.SetMaxOpenConns(25)      // Reasonable limit for analytics queries
	conn.SetMaxIdleConns(5)       // Keep some connections ready
	conn.SetConnMaxLifetime(5 * time.Minute)  // Recycle long-lived connections

	if err := conn.Ping(); 
... (truncated)

     1→# Database Migrations
     2→
     3→This directory contains the database migrations for the v2 version of Flipt.
     4→
     5→We use [golang-migrate](https://github.com/golang-migrate/migrate) to create and manage the migrations.
     6→
     7→Currently the only database supported is Clickhouse for analytics.
     8→
     9→To create a new migration, run the following command:
    10→
    11→```sh
    12→migrate create -ext sql -dir ./migrations/{db} <migration_name>
    13→```
    14→
    15→Where `{db}` is the database type, e.g. `clickhouse`, etc.
    16→
    17→Example:
    18→
    19→```sh
    20→migrate create -ext sql -dir ./migrations/clickhouse create_table_X
    21→```

Flipt config only\n\n#### Environments System\n\n- Environment-per-branch: Map Git branches to environments\n- Environment-per-directory: Organize by microservice/team\n- Environment-per-repository: Separate repos for products\n\n#### APIs\n\n- gRPC API (port 9000) - Primary interface\n- REST API (port 8080) - HTTP gateway over gRPC\n- OpenFeature compatible evaluation\n\n##### Key Endpoints\n\n- **Evaluation API**: `/api/v1/evaluate` - Evaluate feature flags\n- **Management API**: Full CRUD operations on flags, segments, rules\n- **Analytics API**: `/api/v2/analytics` - Flag evaluation metrics\n- **Environments API**: `/api/v2/environments` - Environment management\n- **OFREP API**: `/ofrep/v1` - OpenFeature Remote Evaluation Protocol\n\n#### UI Architecture\n\n- React 19 with TypeScript\n- Redux Toolkit for state management\n- Tailwind CSS for styling\n- Vite for build tooling\n- React Router for navigation\n\n## Development Setup & Commands\n\n### Initial Setup\n\n```bash\n# Install required development tools\nmage bootstrap\n```\n\n### Development Workflow\n\n1. **Setup**: Run `mage bootstrap` to install tools\n2. **Backend Development**:\n   - Use `mage go:run` for server\n   - Server runs on port 8080 (HTTP) and 9000 (gRPC)\n3. **Frontend Development**:\n   - Run `mage ui:run` for UI dev server on port 5173\n   - UI proxies API requests to backend on port 8080\n4. **Full Development**: Run both servers simultaneously\n\n### Build & Run Commands\n\n- `mage build` - Builds the project similar to a release build (default target)\n- `mage go:build` - Builds Go server for development without bundling assets\n- `mage go:run` - Runs Go server in development mode with local config\n- `mage dev` - Alias for go:run\n- `./bin/flipt server --config config/local.yml` - Run built binary with local config\n\n### UI Development Commands\n\n- `mage ui:deps` - Install UI dependencies\n- `mage ui:run` - Run UI in development mode (port 5173)\n- `mage ui:dev` - Alias for ui:run\n- `mage ui:build` - Build UI assets for release\n- `cd ui && npm run dev` - Alternative way to run UI dev server\n\n### Testing Commands\n\n- `mage go:test` - Run all Go unit tests\n- `go test -v {path} -run {test}` - Run a specific Go test\n- `mage go:bench` - Run Go benchmarking tests\n- `mage go:cover` - Run tests and generate coverage report\n- `cd ui && npm run test` - Run UI unit tests (Jest)\n\n### Code Quality Commands\n\n- `mage go:lint` - Run Go linters (golangci-lint and buf lint)\n- `mage go:fmt` - Format Go code with goimports\n- `mage ui:lint` - Run UI linters (ESLint)\n- `mage ui:fmt` - Format UI code (Prettier)\n\n### Code Generation Commands\n\n- `mage go:proto` - Generate protobuf files and gRPC stubs\n- `mage go:mockery` - Generate mocks\n- `mage go:generate` - Generate both mocks and proto files\n\n### Cleanup Commands\n\n- `mage clean` - Clean built files and tidy go.mod\n- `mage prep` - Prepare project for building (clean + ui:build)\n\n### Build Process Notes\n\n- Protocol buffers generate Go and gateway code\n- Mockery generates Go test mocks. See .mockery.yml\n- UI has no code generation\n\n## Code Style Guidelines\n\n### Go Code Style\n\n#### Foundation: Google Go Style Guide\n\n**All Go code should follow the [Google Go Style Guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/go/guide) as the base style guide.**\n\nThe guidelines below are Flipt-specific conventions that build upon the Google style guide. When in doubt, refer to the Google guide first, then apply these project-specific patterns.\n\nKey areas from the Google guide to pay special attention to:\n\n- **Formatting**: Use `gofmt` (we use `goimports` which includes `gofmt`)\n- **Naming**: Follow Go naming conventions for packages, types, functions, and variables\n- **Package organization**: Keep packages focused and avoid circular dependencies\n- **Error handling**: Return errors as the last return value, handle errors explicitly\n- **Documentation**: Write clear godoc comments for exported types and functions\n\n#### Naming Conventions\n\n- **Public functions**: Use PascalCase (`NewServer`, `ListFlags`, `RegisterGRPC`)\n- **Private functions**: Use camelCase (`getStore`, `buildConfig`, `handleError`)\n- **Factory functions**: Use `New` prefix for constructors (`NewRepository`, `NewEnvironmentFactory`)\n- **Variables**: Use camelCase (`environmentKey`, `namespaceKey`, `startTime`)\n- **Constants**: Use PascalCase for exported, camelCase for unexported\n- **Interfaces**: Use descriptive names (`Store`, `EnvironmentStore`, `Validator`)\n\n#### Variable Declarations\n\n```go\n// Prefer := for single variable declarations\nresult := SomeType{}\n\n// Use var blocks for multiple related variables\nvar (\n    environmentKey = r.EnvironmentKey\n    namespaceKey   = r.NamespaceKey\n    startTime      = time.Now().UTC()\n)\n```\n\n#### Constants\n\nUse constants when appropriate for values that are unlikely to change. Even in tests.\n\n**\u274c Bad Examples**\n\n```go\nvar (\n    maxRetries = 3\n    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n)\n```\n\n```go\n  maxRetries := 3\n  secretProvider := \"vault\"\n```\n\n**\u2705 Good Example**\n\n```go\nconst (\n    maxRetries = 3\n    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n)\n```\n\n#### Error Handling\n\n##### Error Types\n\nUse the custom error types when possible:\n\n```go\n// Preferred - use custom error types\nreturn nil, errs.ErrNotFoundf(\"flag %q not found\", key)\nreturn nil, errs.ErrInvalidf(\"invalid configuration: %s\", reason)\n\n// Fallback - standard error handling\nreturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to process: %w\", err)\n```\n\n##### Inline Errors\n\nPrefer inline error declarations and checking when it makes sense.\n\n**\u274c Bad Example**\n\n```go\nerr := doSomething()\nif err != nil {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**\u2705 Good Example**\n\n```go\nif err := doSomething(); err != nil {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Imports\n\nFollow the three-group import pattern (extends Google guide):\n\n```go\nimport (\n    // Standard library\n    \"context\"\n    \"fmt\"\n    \"time\"\n\n    // Third-party packages\n    \"github.com/go-git/go-git/v6\"\n    \"go.uber.org/zap\"\n\n    // Local packages\n    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/errors\"\n    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config\"\n)\n```\n\n#### Logging\n\nUse structured logging with zap:\n\n```go\n// Preferred - structured logging with context\ns.logger.Debug(\"processing request\", \n    zap.String(\"environment\", envKey),\n    zap.String(\"namespace\", nsKey),\n    zap.Int(\"count\", len(items)))\n\n// Use appropriate log levels\ns.logger.Debug(\"debug info for development\")  // Most common\ns.logger.Info(\"important application events\")\ns.logger.Warn(\"recoverable error conditions\")\ns.logger.Error(\"error conditions that need attention\")\n\n// Avoid overusing log statements - be selective about what to log\n```\n\n#### Comments and Documentation\n\n```go\n// Public functions need godoc comments starting with function name\n// ListFlags lists all flags in the specified environment and namespace\nfunc (s *Server) ListFlags(ctx context.Context, r *flipt.ListFlagRequest) (*flipt.FlagList, error) {\n    // Inline comments explain complex logic\n    // Check for X-Environment header for backward compatibility\n    environmentKey := r.EnvironmentKey\n    if headerEnv, ok := common.FliptEnvironmentFromContext(ctx); ok && headerEnv != \"\" {\n        environmentKey = headerEnv\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Project Organization\n\n- Use `internal/` for private packages that shouldn't be imported externally\n- Organize by domain (`server/`, `storage/`, `config/`, `analytics/`)\n- Keep interfaces in domain root, implementations in subdirectories\n- Co-locate tests with implementation (`*_test.go`)\n- Use `testdata/` directories for test fixtures\n\n#### Pre-commit Quality Checks (Go)\n\n**Always run these commands when adding or editing Go code:**\n\n```bash\n# Format Go code\nmage go:fmt\n\n# Lint Go code\nmage go:lint\n\n# Run modernize to update code to 1.24+ style\nmage go:modernize\n```\n\n### UI/React/TypeScript Code Style\n\n#### File Naming and Organization\n\n- **Components**: Use PascalCase for `.tsx` files (`FlagForm.tsx`, `FlagTable.tsx`)\n- **API files**: Use camelCase with suffix (`flagsApi.ts`, `authApi.ts`)\n- **Types**: Use PascalCase for `.ts` files (`Flag.ts`, `Analytics.ts`)\n- **Utilities**: Use descriptive lowercase names (`helpers.ts`)\n\n#### Component Structure\n\n- Use functional components with hooks\n- Organize components by domain in directories\n- Keep reusable UI components in `ui/` directory\n- Co-locate component tests with implementation\n\n#### State Management\n\n- Use Redux Toolkit for application state\n- Create API slices for domain-specific data (`flagsApi.ts`)\n- Use TypeScript for type safety throughout\n\n#### Pre-commit Quality Checks (UI)\n\n**Always run these commands when adding or editing UI code:**\n\n```bash\n# Format UI code (TypeScript/React)\nmage ui:fmt\n\n# Lint UI code (ESLint)\nmage ui:lint\n```\n\n### General Pre-commit Checks\n\n```bash\n# Format specific markdown files (replace with actual filename)\nnpx prettier -w README.md\n```\n\n## Configuration\n\n### Configuration Files\n\n- `config/local.yml` - Local development config\n- `config/dev.yml` - Alternative dev config\n- User config at `{{ USER_CONFIG_DIR }}/flipt/config.yml`\n\n### Debugging Tips\n\n- Use `FLIPT_LOG_LEVEL=debug` for verbose logging\n- Check `/metrics` endpoint for Prometheus metrics\n- View OpenTelemetry traces for request flow\n- Git sync issues: Check repository access and credentials\n- Authentication issues: Verify redirect URLs and client configurations\n\n## Testing Guidelines\n\n### Test Structure\n\n- Go tests use testcontainers for unit tests that depend on external tools\n- UI tests use Jest for unit tests and Playwright for E2E\n\n### Writing Effective Tests\n\nWhen writing tests, ensure they actually verify the functionality being tested:\n\n**\u274c Bad Example - Test doesn't verify actual behavior:**\n\n```go\n// This test only verifies the method runs without error, not that the logic works\nfunc TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n    require.NoError(t, err)\n    assert.NotNil(t, result)\n}\n```\n\n**\u2705 Good Example - Test verifies specific behavior:**\n\n```go\n// This test verifies the actual logic and behavior\nfunc TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    // Use mock.MatchedBy to verify the correct data is passed through\n    store.On(\"Method\", mock.MatchedBy(func(ctx context.Context) bool {\n        // Verify the context contains the expected values\n        value, ok := somePackage.ValueFromContext(ctx)\n        return ok && value == expectedValue\n    }), expectedArg).Return(expectedResult, nil)\n    \n    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n    require.NoError(t, err)\n    \n    // Verify the actual business logic worked correctly\n    assert.Equal(t, expectedOutput, result.ImportantField)\n    store.AssertExpectations(t) // Ensures mocks were called as expected\n}\n```\n\n**Key Testing Principles:**\n\n- **Verify behavior, not just success**: Don't just check that methods return without error\n- **Test the logic**: Use `mock.MatchedBy` to verify correct data flows through the system\n- **Test edge cases**: Include tests for when conditions are met vs. not met\n- **Use meaningful assertions**: Assert on the specific values that matter to the business logic\n- **Mock verification**: Use `mock.AssertExpectations(t)` to ensure mocks were called with expected parameters\n\n### Integration Tests\n\nIntegration tests are defined in `build/testing/` and run as Mage targets. For details on available integration test targets, helpers, and how to add new integration tests, see the files in that directory:\n\n- `build/testing/integration.go` - Integration test Mage targets and configuration\n- `build/testing/integration/` - Individual integration test suites\n- `build/testing/helpers.go` - Shared test helpers\n- `build/testing/test.go` - Core test utilities\n\n## Git Workflow & Commits\n\n### Creating Effective Commits\n\n#### Commit Message Format\n\nFollow conventional commit format:\n\n```\ntype(scope): brief description\n\nLonger description if needed explaining the why, not the what.\n\n- List specific changes if helpful\n- Include any breaking changes\n- Reference issues (e.g., \"Fixes #123\")\n```\n\n#### Commit Types\n\n- `feat:` - New features\n- `fix:` - Bug fixes\n- `docs:` - Documentation changes\n- `style:` - Code style changes (formatting, etc.)\n- `refactor:` - Code refactoring without functional changes\n- `test:` - Adding or modifying tests\n- `chore:` - Build process or auxiliary tool changes\n\n#### Examples\n\n```bash\n# Good commit messages\ngit commit -s -m \"feat: add X-Environment header support to ListFlags endpoint\n\nThe v1 ListFlags endpoint now checks for X-Environment header \nfor backward compatibility. When present, the header value \ntakes precedence over the request environment parameter.\n\n- Modified ListFlags method to check context for environment header\n- Added ForwardFliptEnvironment middleware to v1 API gateway\n- Added comprehensive test coverage\n\nFixes #4411\"\n\ngit commit -s -m \"fix: resolve race condition in flag evaluation cache\"\n\ngit commit -s -m \"test: improve X-Environment header test coverage\n\n- Use mock.MatchedBy to verify context contains correct environment\n- Add test for when header is not present\n- Ensure tests actually validate the header precedence logic\"\n```\n\n### Pull Request Guidelines\n\n#### PR Title Format\n\nUse the same conventional commit format for PR titles:\n\n```\ntype(scope): brief description\n```\n\n#### PR Description Template\n\n```markdown\n## Summary\n\nBrief description of what this PR does and why.\n\n## Changes\n\n- **Modified `file1.go`**: Specific change description\n- **Added `file2_test.go`**: Test coverage description\n- **Updated `config.yml`**: Configuration change description\n\n## Backward Compatibility\n\nDescribe any backward compatibility or breaking change considerations.\n\n## Additional Notes\n\nAny other context, screenshots, or related issues.\n```\n\n#### PR Best Practices\n\n- **Keep PRs focused**: One logical change per PR\n- **Write descriptive titles**: Use conventional commit format\n- **Provide context**: Explain the \"why\" behind changes\n- **Include tests**: Always add tests for new functionality\n- **Run quality checks**: Format and lint before creating PR\n- **Reference issues**: Use \"Fixes #123\" to auto-close issues\n- **Review your own PR**: Look through the diff before requesting review\n- **Base PRs on the correct branch**: Base PRs on the correct branch (e.g. `v2` for v2 changes, `main` for v1 changes)\n- **Label PRs correctly**: When creating a feature based off of the v2 branch, label the PR with the `v2` label. Similarly for a v1 (main) feature, use the `v1` label.\n\n#### Quality Checklist\n\nBefore creating a PR, ensure:\n\n- [ ] Code follows style guidelines\n- [ ] Tests are added and passing\n- [ ] Linting passes (`mage go:lint` / `mage ui:lint`)\n- [ ] Code is formatted (`mage go:fmt` / `mage ui:fmt`)\n- [ ] Commit messages are clear and descriptive\n- [ ] PR description explains the change and its purpose\n",

Focus ONLY on efficiency issues: unnecessary work, performance problems, and scalability concerns.\n\n## Changes Summary\n\nNew CockroachDB analytics backend implementation with:\n- Connection pooling via database/sql\n- Migration handling with golang-migrate\n- Query execution for flag evaluation analytics\n- SQL aggregation queries\n\n## Task\n\nReview for efficiency issues:\n\n1. **Unnecessary work**:\n   - Redundant computations (e.g., calculating time windows multiple times)\n   - Repeated file reads or data lookups\n   - Unnecessary type conversions\n\n2. **Connection and pooling**:\n   - Is sql.Open configured properly for connection pooling?\n   - Missing connection pool size settings?\n   - Unnecessary Ping() calls that could cause latency?\n\n3. **Query efficiency**:\n   - N+1 query patterns?\n   - Inefficient query logic (e.g., large GROUP BY operations)?\n   - Missing query parameters/prepared statements?\n   - Unbounded result sets?\n\n4. **Missed opportunities for concurrency**:\n   - Can independent operations run in parallel?\n   - Is sync.Once appropriate and safe?\n\n5. **Hot-path bloat**:\n   - Is blocking work being added to startup (migrations)?\n   - Are migrations forced unnecessarily?\n\n6. **Memory issues**:\n   - Unbounded slices/arrays being allocated?\n   - Memory leaks from connections or resources?\n   - Unnecessary data copies?\n\n7. **Startup performance**:\n   - Is dbOnce.Do() efficient for one-time initialization?\n   - Should migrations be optional or async?\n\n## Specific Questions\n\n- Will the SQL queries perform well on large datasets? (e.g., millions of rows)\n- Are there indexes on the table columns being queried? (check migration files)\n- Is the time bucketing calculation efficient (EXTRACT/DATE_TRUNC)?\n- Should LIMIT be enforced at the query level (already done?)?\n- Are connection parameters optimized for analytics workloads?\n\nFor each finding:\n- Describe the inefficiency\n- Impact: HIGH (significant perf impact), MEDIUM (noticeable), LOW (negligible)\n- Suggest optimization\n",

      "text": "Perfect. Now I have all the information I need to write a comprehensive efficiency review. Let me create the report:\n\n## Code Efficiency Review: Flipt CockroachDB Analytics Backend\n\nI've completed a thorough analysis of the CockroachDB analytics backend implementation. Below are my efficiency findings organized by category and severity.\n\n---\n\n## 1. CRITICAL EFFICIENCY ISSUES\n\n### Issue 1.1: Missing Connection Pool Configuration\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 66-77)\n\n**Problem**: \nThe `connect()` function uses `sql.Open()` without configuring connection pool parameters:\n```go\nfunc connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {\n\tconn, err := sql.Open(\"postgres\", cfg.URL)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tif err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn conn, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe default connection pool settings in Go's `database/sql` are:\n- `MaxOpenConns`: unlimited (can cause resource exhaustion)\n- `MaxIdleConns`: 2 (too low for analytics workloads)\n- `ConnMaxLifetime`: unlimited (connections not recycled)\n\n**Impact**: **HIGH** - For analytics workloads with multiple concurrent queries, this will:\n- Create unbounded connections under load\n- Exhaust database connection limits\n- Cause connection pool starvation\n- Lead to cascading failures\n\n**Recommendation**:\n```go\nfunc connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {\n\tconn, err := sql.Open(\"postgres\", cfg.URL)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\t// Configure connection pool for analytics workloads\n\tconn.SetMaxOpenConns(25)      // Reasonable limit for analytics queries\n\tconn.SetMaxIdleConns(5)       // Keep some connections ready\n\tconn.SetConnMaxLifetime(5 * time.Minute)  // Recycle long-lived connections\n\n\tif err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn conn, nil\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Issue 1.2: Unbounded Slice Allocations in Hot Path\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 117-135 and 180-204)\n\n**Problem**:\nIn `GetFlagEvaluationsCount()` and `GetBatchFlagEvaluationsCount()`, slices are initialized with zero capacity and grown via `append()`:\n\n```go\nvar (\n    timestamps = make([]string, 0)  // Zero capacity - inefficient for growth\n    values     = make([]float32, 0)\n)\n\nfor rows.Next() {\n    // ... \n    timestamps.append(timestamps, timestamp)  // Causes repeated allocations\n    values.append(values, float32(value))\n}\n```\n\nEach `append()` that exceeds capacity triggers a reallocation (typically doubling capacity). For large datasets (millions of analytics records), this causes:\n- Repeated memory allocations\n- Garbage collection pressure\n- Cache misses\n\n**Impact**: **MEDIUM-HIGH** - Noticeable performance degradation with large result sets.\n\n**Recommendation**:\nPre-allocate with capacity hints from the query or use an estimated upper bound:\n\n```go\n// Option 1: If the row count is known or can be estimated\ntimestamps := make([]string, 0, estimatedCapacity)\nvalues := make([]float32, 0, estimatedCapacity)\n\n// Option 2: Common pattern - allocate with a reasonable initial size\ntimestamps := make([]string, 0, 100)  // Common case: 100 data points\nvalues := make([]float32, 0, 100)\n```\n\nAlternatively, use `append` once before the loop if you can afford to read all rows:\n```go\n// Collect into temp slice first, then allocate exact size\nvar tempTimestamps []string\nvar tempValues []float32\nfor rows.Next() {\n    // append to temp slices\n}\ntimestamps := tempTimestamps  // Now allocation is done once\nvalues := tempValues\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. QUERY EFFICIENCY ISSUES\n\n### Issue 2.1: Inefficient Time Bucketing Calculation\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 88-91, 148)\n\n**Problem**:\nThe time bucketing calculation is inefficient:\n```sql\nEXTRACT(EPOCH FROM DATE_TRUNC('minute', timestamp))::bigint / ($4 * 60) * ($4 * 60) AS timestamp_bucket\n```\n\nThis query:\n1. Converts timestamp to EPOCH (seconds since 1970)\n2. Divides by `StepMinutes * 60` (the computation happens at runtime for EVERY row)\n3. Multiplies back by `StepMinutes * 60`\n\nThe CPU-intensive arithmetic is performed for every row in the result set. For millions of rows, this is wasteful.\n\n**Additional Problem** (line 148):\nAfter getting the bucketed timestamp from the database, the application recalculates it again:\n```go\ntimestamp := time.Unix(timestampBucket, 0).UTC().Format(time.DateTime)\n```\n\nThis is redundant work: the database already computed the bucket, and then the application converts it back to a formatted string, doing extra work.\n\n**Impact**: **MEDIUM** - Scales poorly with dataset size. The calculation is repeated millions of times.\n\n**Recommendation**:\nLet the database format the timestamp more efficiently:\n\n```sql\n-- Instead of arithmetic, use DATE_TRUNC directly with the interval\nSELECT\n    DATE_TRUNC('minute', timestamp) AS timestamp_bucket,\n    SUM(value) AS value\nFROM flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2\nWHERE environment_key = $1 \n  AND namespace_key = $2 \n  AND flag_key = $3 \n  AND timestamp >= $4 \n  AND timestamp < $5\nGROUP BY DATE_TRUNC('minute', timestamp)\nORDER BY timestamp_bucket ASC\n```\n\nIf variable step bucketing is needed, use:\n```sql\n-- For 5-minute buckets, for example\nDATE_TRUNC('minute', timestamp + interval '2 minutes 30 seconds')\n  AT TIME ZONE 'UTC' - interval '2 minutes 30 seconds'\n```\n\nOr pre-calculate the bucket width in the application and pass it as a parameter (less CPU in DB).\n\n---\n\n### Issue 2.2: Missing LIMIT Enforcement in Single-Flag Query\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 88-101)\n\n**Problem**:\n`GetFlagEvaluationsCount()` has no LIMIT clause. If a user requests analytics for a very wide time window (e.g., 1 year), the query will fetch potentially millions of rows into memory:\n\n```sql\nSELECT\n    EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM DATE_TRUNC('minute', timestamp))::bigint / ($4 * 60) * ($4 * 60) AS timestamp_bucket,\n    SUM(value) AS value\nFROM flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2\nWHERE environment_key = $1 AND namespace_key = $2 AND flag_key = $3 AND ...\nGROUP BY timestamp_bucket\nORDER BY timestamp_bucket ASC\n-- NO LIMIT!\n```\n\n**Impact**: **MEDIUM** - Unbounded memory usage on large time windows.\n\n**Recommendation**:\nAdd a reasonable LIMIT (e.g., 1440 data points = 1 day of 1-minute data). For requests exceeding this, the client can implement pagination or request larger time steps:\n\n```go\nconst maxDataPoints = 1440  // 1 day of minute-granularity data\n\nrows, err := c.Conn.QueryContext(ctx, `\n    SELECT ... \n    GROUP BY timestamp_bucket\n    ORDER BY timestamp_bucket ASC\n    LIMIT $6\n`,\n    req.EnvironmentKey,\n    req.NamespaceKey,\n    req.FlagKey,\n    req.StepMinutes,\n    req.From,\n    req.To,\n    maxDataPoints,\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n### Issue 2.3: Suboptimal Batch Query with ANY() and LIMIT\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 154, 159)\n\n**Problem**:\nThe batch query uses `flag_key = ANY($7)` which may not use indexes efficiently in all cases:\n\n```sql\nWHERE\n    environment_key = $1 AND\n    namespace_key = $2 AND\n    flag_key = ANY($7) AND  -- May have suboptimal index plan\n    timestamp >= $5 AND\n    timestamp < $6\n```\n\nAdditionally, `LIMIT $8` is applied AFTER the GROUP BY and ORDER BY, which means:\n1. All matching rows are grouped and aggregated\n2. All results are sorted\n3. Only then is the LIMIT applied\n\nFor 1000 flags with months of data, this aggregates massive amounts of data before discarding most of it.\n\n**Impact**: **MEDIUM** - Query planner may choose suboptimal execution paths; unnecessary aggregation work.\n\n**Recommendation**:\n1. Create a composite index on `(environment_key, namespace_key, flag_key, timestamp)` in migrations\n2. Push the limit down earlier in the query:\n\n```sql\n-- Better: Use DISTINCT ON or window functions to get top N per flag\nWITH ranked_data AS (\n    SELECT\n        flag_key,\n        EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM DATE_TRUNC('minute', timestamp))::bigint / ($4 * 60) * ($4 * 60) AS timestamp_bucket,\n        SUM(value) AS value,\n        ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY flag_key ORDER BY timestamp_bucket DESC) AS rn\n    FROM flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2\n    WHERE environment_key = $1 \n      AND namespace_key = $2 \n      AND flag_key = ANY($7) \n      AND timestamp >= $5 \n      AND timestamp < $6\n    GROUP BY flag_key, timestamp_bucket\n)\nSELECT flag_key, timestamp_bucket, value\nFROM ranked_data\nWHERE rn <= $8  -- Limit per flag, not total\nORDER BY flag_key, timestamp_bucket ASC\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. MEMORY AND DATA HANDLING ISSUES\n\n### Issue 3.1: Inefficient Batch Query Result Processing\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 141-204)\n\n**Problem**:\nIn `GetBatchFlagEvaluationsCount()`, the code creates intermediate objects for every row:\n\n```go\ndata := result[flagKey]\ndata.Timestamps = append(data.Timestamps, timestamp)\ndata.Values = append(data.Values, float32(value))\nresult[flagKey] = data  // Unnecessary copy back to map\n```\n\nThis pattern:\n1. Retrieves the struct from the map (copy)\n2. Modifies the copy\n3. Writes it back to the map (another copy)\n\nThis is inefficient for large result sets. Each row incurs unnecessary memory copies.\n\n**Impact**: **LOW-MEDIUM** - Constant factor overhead on memory operations.\n\n**Recommendation**:\nStore pointers in the map or use direct field access:\n\n```go\n// Option 1: Use pointers\nresult := make(map[string]*analytics.FlagEvaluationData)\n\nfor rows.Next() {\n    // ...\n    if _, ok := result[flagKey]; !ok {\n        result[flagKey] = &analytics.FlagEvaluationData{\n            Timestamps: make([]string, 0),\n            Values:     make([]float32, 0),\n        }\n    }\n    \n    result[flagKey].Timestamps = append(result[flagKey].Timestamps, timestamp)\n    result[flagKey].Values = append(result[flagKey].Values, float32(value))\n}\n\n// Then convert to non-pointer map before returning\nflagData := make(map[string]analytics.FlagEvaluationData)\nfor key, data := range result {\n    flagData[key] = *data\n}\nreturn flagData, nil\n```\n\n---\n\n### Issue 3.2: Unnecessary Ping() Call in Startup Path\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (line 72) and `/workspace/flipt/internal/storage/analytics/db.go` (line 34)\n\n**Problem**:\nThere are TWO separate `Ping()` calls in sequence:\n1. In `db.go` `open()` function (line 34)\n2. In `client.go` `connect()` function (line 72)\n\nBoth execute during the one-time initialization in `dbOnce.Do()`:\n\n```go\n// In db.go\nif err := db.Ping(); err != nil {\n    return nil, \"\", fmt.Errorf(\"failed to ping CockroachDB: %w\", err)\n}\n```\n\n```go\n// In client.go \nif err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {\n    return nil, err\n}\n```\n\n`Ping()` adds latency to startup. With two pings, startup is unnecessarily slow.\n\n**Impact**: **LOW** - Affects startup time only (not hot path), but unnecessary.\n\n**Recommendation**:\nRemove one redundant Ping call. If checking connectivity is important, do it once in `connect()`:\n\n```go\n// In client.go - this is sufficient\nfunc connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {\n    conn, err := sql.Open(\"postgres\", cfg.URL)\n    if err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n\n    // Only ping here\n    if err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n\n    return conn, nil\n}\n\n// Remove the second ping from db.go\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. INITIALIZATION AND STARTUP ISSUES\n\n### Issue 4.1: Blocking Migration in Synchronous Initialization\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 29-43)\n\n**Problem**:\nThe `New()` constructor uses `sync.Once.Do()` to run migrations synchronously:\n\n```go\nvar dbOnce sync.Once\n\nfunc New(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) (*Client, error) {\n    var conn *sql.DB\n    var cockroachErr error\n\n    dbOnce.Do(func() {\n        err := runMigrations(logger, cfg, forceMigrate)  // Blocks startup\n        if err != nil {\n            cockroachErr = err\n            return\n        }\n        // ... connection establishment\n    })\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\nIf this is called from the gRPC server startup (`grpc.go`), it blocks the entire server from starting. For a server with large databases, migrations can take seconds or minutes.\n\n**Impact**: **MEDIUM** - Startup latency adds to deployment time; if migrations fail, the entire server fails to start.\n\n**Recommendation**:\n1. Run migrations separately from server startup (already available via `flipt migrate` CLI)\n2. Or, check if migrations are up-to-date but don't force them:\n\n```go\n// In migrator.go - only check version, don't auto-migrate\nfunc (m *Migrator) UpIfNeeded() error {\n    currentVersion, _, err := m.migrator.Version()\n    if err != nil {\n        if !errors.Is(err, migrate.ErrNilVersion) {\n            return fmt.Errorf(\"checking migrations: %w\", err)\n        }\n        // First run - fail with helpful message\n        return errors.New(\"no migrations found - please run 'flipt migrate' first\")\n    }\n\n    expectedVersion := expectedVersions[m.driver]\n    if currentVersion < expectedVersion {\n        return fmt.Errorf(\"migrations out of date: current=%d, expected=%d - please run 'flipt migrate'\", \n            currentVersion, expectedVersion)\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Issue 4.2: sync.Once Usage with Error Handling Anti-pattern\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go` (lines 16, 29-47)\n\n**Problem**:\nUsing `sync.Once` with error handling is awkward:\n\n```go\nvar dbOnce sync.Once\n\nfunc New(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) (*Client, error) {\n    var (\n        conn          *sql.DB\n        cockroachErr  error  // Must declare outside to capture error\n    )\n\n    dbOnce.Do(func() {\n        // ... error handling inside closure\n        cockroachErr = err\n        return\n    })\n\n    if cockroachErr != nil {\n        return nil, cockroachErr\n    }\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\nThis pattern is fragile:\n- If `cockroachErr` is not initialized before the first call fails, the error is lost\n- The error type is awkward (interface{} -> error)\n- Similar pattern used in ClickHouse client as well (code duplication)\n\n**Impact**: **LOW** - Maintainability issue; potential for hidden bugs if error handling is refactored.\n\n**Recommendation**:\nUse a cleaner pattern with `sync.Once` + pointer to result:\n\n```go\nvar (\n    dbOnce   sync.Once\n    dbResult *dbInitResult\n)\n\ntype dbInitResult struct {\n    conn  *sql.DB\n    err   error\n}\n\nfunc New(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) (*Client, error) {\n    dbOnce.Do(func() {\n        conn, err := initDB(logger, cfg, forceMigrate)\n        dbResult = &dbInitResult{conn: conn, err: err}\n    })\n\n    if dbResult.err != nil {\n        return nil, dbResult.err\n    }\n\n    return &Client{Conn: dbResult.conn}, nil\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. INDEX COVERAGE ISSUES\n\n### Issue 5.1: Potentially Missing Composite Index\n**File**: `/workspace/flipt/internal/migrations/cockroachdb/20250121202326_create_table_counter_aggregated_analytics.up.sql`\n\n**Problem**:\nThe migration creates individual indexes but may not have an optimal composite index for query patterns:\n\n```sql\nCREATE INDEX idx_flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2_env_ns_flag \n    ON flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2 (environment_key, namespace_key, flag_key);\n\nCREATE INDEX idx_flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2_timestamp \n    ON flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2 (timestamp);\n```\n\nBoth queries filter on `(environment_key, namespace_key, flag_key, timestamp)`, but the indexes are separate. CockroachDB may use the first index and then filter on timestamp, or vice versa, resulting in suboptimal performance.\n\n**Impact**: **MEDIUM** - Queries will still work but may scan many unnecessary rows before filtering.\n\n**Recommendation**:\nAdd a composite index that covers the query's WHERE clause:\n\n```sql\n-- In the migration file, add:\nCREATE INDEX idx_flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2_env_ns_flag_ts \n    ON flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_v2 (environment_key, namespace_key, flag_key, timestamp);\n```\n\nThis allows the database to jump directly to matching rows without filtering.\n\n---\n\n## 6. COMPARISON WITH CLICKHOUSE IMPLEMENTATION\n\nInterestingly, the ClickHouse implementation (`clickhouse/client.go`) has better efficiency patterns:\n\n1. **ClickHouse benefits**:\n   - Uses `fmt.Sprintf()` to dynamically build queries (not ideal for SQL injection, but shows flexibility)\n   - Better handling of pre-allocation using intermediate maps\n   - Has data downsampling logic (lines 269-273) for respecting limits\n   - Uses `WITH FILL` to guarantee uniform intervals in results\n\n2. **CockroachDB missing features**:\n   - No downsampling/result limiting per-flag\n   - No guaranteed uniform intervals (ClickHouse's `WITH FILL`)\n   - Weaker handling of large result sets\n\n---\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Issue | Severity | Impact | Category |\n|-------|----------|--------|----------|\n| Missing connection pool config | HIGH | Resource exhaustion, cascading failures | Connection Pooling |\n| Unbounded slice allocations | MEDIUM-HIGH | Large result set slow-downs, GC pressure | Memory |\n| Inefficient time bucketing | MEDIUM | Scales poorly with dataset size | Query Efficiency |\n| Missing LIMIT in single-flag query | MEDIUM | Unbounded memory usage | Query Efficiency |\n| Suboptimal batch query LIMIT | MEDIUM | Unnecessary aggregation work | Query Efficiency |\n| Inefficient result processing (copies) | LOW-MEDIUM | Memory overhead on large sets | Memory |\n| Redundant Ping() calls | LOW | Startup latency | Startup |\n| Blocking migrations in startup | MEDIUM | Deployment delays | Startup |\n| sync.Once error pattern | LOW | Maintainability risk | Code Quality |\n| Missing composite index | MEDIUM | Suboptimal query plans | Indexing |\n\n---\n\n## Immediate Action Items\n\n**Priority 1 (Critical)**:\n1. // open is a convenience function of providing a database.sql instance for
// an analytics database.
func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
		clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
		if err != nil {
			return nil, "", err
		}

		db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)

		return db, Clickhouse, nil
	}

	return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
}
After
// open is a convenience function of providing a database.sql instance for
// an analytics database.
func open(cfg config.Config) (*sql.DB, Driver, error) {
	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
		clickhouseOptions, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
		if err != nil {
			return nil, "", err
		}

		db := clickhouse.OpenDB(clickhouseOptions)

		return db, Clickhouse, nil
	}

	if cfg.Analytics.Storage.CockroachDB.Enabled {
		db, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.Analytics.Storage.CockroachDB.URL)
		if err != nil {
			return nil, "", fmt.Errorf("failed to open CockroachDB connection: %w", err)
		}

		if err := db.Ping(); err != nil {
			return nil, "", fmt.Errorf("failed to ping CockroachDB: %w", err)
		}

		return db, CockroachDB, nil
	}

	return nil, "", errors.New("no analytics db provided")
}

6. EDIT /workspace/flipt/internal/storage/analytics/migrator.go
Before
// NewMigrator returns a migrator for analytics databases
func NewMigrator(cfg config.Config, logger *zap.Logger) (*Migrator, error) {
	sql, driver, err := open(cfg)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("opening db: %w", err)
	}

	var dr database.Driver

	if driver == Clickhouse {
		options, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
		if err != nil {
			return nil, err
		}

		dr, err = clickhouseMigrate.WithInstance(sql, &clickhouseMigrate.Config{
			DatabaseName:          options.Auth.Database,
			MigrationsTableEngine: "MergeTree",
		})
		if err != nil {
			return nil, fmt.Errorf("getting db driver for: %s: %w", driver, err)
		}
	}

	logger.Debug("using driver", zap.String("driver", driver.String()))

	return migratorHelper(logger, sql, driver, dr)
}
After
// NewMigrator returns a migrator for analytics databases
func NewMigrator(cfg config.Config, logger *zap.Logger) (*Migrator, error) {
	sql, driver, err := open(cfg)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("opening db: %w", err)
	}

	var dr database.Driver

	if driver == Clickhouse {
		options, err := cfg.Analytics.Storage.Clickhouse.Options()
		if err != nil {
			return nil, err
		}

		dr, err = clickhouseMigrate.WithInstance(sql, &clickhouseMigrate.Config{
			DatabaseName:          options.Auth.Database,
			MigrationsTableEngine: "MergeTree",
		})
		if err != nil {
			return nil, fmt.Errorf("getting db driver for: %s: %w", driver, err)
		}
	} else if driver == CockroachDB {
		dr, err = postgresMigrate.WithInstance(sql, &postgresMigrate.Config{})
		if err != nil {
			return nil, fmt.Errorf("getting db driver for: %s: %w", driver, err)
		}
	}

	logger.Debug("using driver", zap.String("driver", driver.String()))

	return migratorHelper(logger, sql, driver, dr)
}

CREATE VIEW flipt_counter_aggregated_analytics_mv_v2 AS
SELECT
    timestamp,
    analytic_name,
    environment_key,
    namespace_key,
    flag_key,
    reason,
    evaluation_value,
    SUM(value) AS value
FROM flipt_counter_analytics_v2
GROUP BY
    timestamp,
    analytic_name,
    environment_key,
    namespace_key,
    flag_key,
    reason,
    evaluation_value;

func (a *AnalyticsConfig) validate() error {
	if a.Storage.Clickhouse.Enabled {
		if a.Storage.Clickhouse.URL == "" {
			return errFieldRequired("analytics", "clickhouse url")
		}

		if a.Buffer.FlushPeriod < time.Second*10 {
			return errString("analytics", "buffer flush period below 10 seconds")
		}
	}

	if a.Storage.CockroachDB.Enabled {
		if a.Storage.CockroachDB.URL == "" {
			return errFieldRequired("analytics", "cockroachdb url")
		}

		if a.Buffer.FlushPeriod < time.Second*10 {
			return errString("analytics", "buffer flush period below 10 seconds")
		}
	}

	return nil
}

19. WRITE /workspace/flipt/internal/server/analytics/cockroachdb/client.go
package cockroachdb

import (
	"context"
	"database/sql"
	"fmt"
	"sync"
	"time"

	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config"
	"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/server/analytics"
	analyticsstorage "go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/storage/analytics"
	"go.uber.org/zap"
)

var dbOnce sync.Once

type Client struct {
	Conn *sql.DB
}

// New constructs a new CockroachDB client that conforms to the analytics.Client contract.
func New(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) (*Client, error) {
	var (
		conn          *sql.DB
		cockroachErr  error
	)

	dbOnce.Do(func() {
		err := runMigrations(logger, cfg, forceMigrate)
		if err != nil {
			cockroachErr = err
			return
		}

		connection, err := connect(cfg.Analytics.Storage.CockroachDB)
		if err != nil {
			cockroachErr = err
			return
		}

		conn = connection
	})

	if cockroachErr != nil {
		return nil, cockroachErr
	}

	return &Client{Conn: conn}, nil
}

// runMigrations will run migrations for CockroachDB.
func runMigrations(logger *zap.Logger, cfg *config.Config, forceMigrate bool) error {
	m, err := analyticsstorage.NewMigrator(*cfg, logger)
	if err != nil {
		return err
	}

	if err := m.Up(forceMigrate); err != nil {
		return err
	}

	return nil
}

func connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {
	conn, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.URL)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	if err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	return conn, nil
}

func (c *Client) String() string {
	return "cockroachdb"
}

	// Calculate the time window based on step
	stepDuration := time.Duration(r

				return nil, fmt.Errorf("connecting to cockroachdb: %w", err)
			}
			analyticsExporter := analytics.NewAnalyticsSinkSpanExporter(logger, client)
			tracingProvider.RegisterSpanProcessor(
				tracesdk.NewBatchSpanProcessor(
					analyticsExporter,
					tracesdk.WithBatchTimeout(cfg.Analytics.Buffer.FlushPeriod)),
			)
			server.onShutdown(func(ctx context.Context) error {
				return analyticsExporter.Shutdown(ctx)
			})
			rpcanalytics.RegisterAnalyticsServiceServer(handlers, analytics.New(logger, client))
			logger.Debug("analytics enabled", zap.String("database", client.String()), zap.String("flush_period", cfg.Analytics.Buffer.FlushPeriod.String()))
		} else if cfg.Analytics.Storage.Prometheus.Enabled {
			client, err := prometheus.New(logger, cfg)
			if err != nil {
				return nil, err
			}

func connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {
	conn, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.URL)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	if err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	return conn, nil
}

After
func connect(cfg config.CockroachDBConfig) (*sql.DB, error) {
	conn, err := sql.Open("postgres", cfg.URL)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	// Configure connection pool for analytics workloads
	conn.SetMaxOpenConns(25)
	conn.SetMaxIdleConns(5)
	conn.SetConnMaxLifetime(5 * time.Minute)

	if err := conn.Ping(); err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	return conn, nil
}

func (c *Client) String() string {
	return "cockroachdb"
}

// Close closes the database connection.
func (c *Client) Close() error {
	if c != nil && c.Conn != nil {
		return c.Conn.Close()
	}
	return nil
}
